{"step_index":742,"source":"MODEL","type":"PLANNER_RESPONSE","status":"DONE","created_at":"2026-05-10T07:31:08Z","content":"This is a classic product design question for fitness and wellness apps! Here are the pros and cons of both, and what I recommend:\n\n### 1. Counting from \"Day 1\" (Program-Based)\n*   **Pros**: It is **highly motivating**. Seeing \"Day 45 of 90\" gives a strong sense of progress and accomplishment. It feels like a journey or a course you are completing.\n*   **Cons**: You lose the context of the actual day of the week, which matters for planning (e.g., \"I need to prep meals on Sunday\").\n\n### 2. Using the Actual Calendar (Date-Based)\n*   **Pros**: It helps users ground their habits in real-world time. They know exactly what day it is and can plan around their real life (work, weekends, etc.).\n*   **Cons**: \"June 24\" doesn't tell me how far I've come on my fitness journey.\n\n---\n\n### My Recommendation: **The Hybrid Approach**\nThe best approach (and what we just built!) is to combine them:\n*   Make the **Program Day (e.g., \"Day 2\")** the big, important number at the top. This is the focus.\n<truncated 289 bytes>"}

When you access the app from your computer, `localhost` works fine. {"step_index":2135,"source":"MODEL","type":"PLANNER_RESPONSE","status":"DONE","created_at":"2026-05-11T01:52:12Z","content":"I understand! On mobile phones, the standard `100vh` setting sometimes leaves a small gap at the top or bottom because of the browser's address bar or the phone's status bar (where the battery and time are).\n\nI have fixed this by doing two things:\n1.  I changed the height to **`100dvh`** (Dynamic Viewport Height).
